Currently usage limits do not apply to Salt or foreign managed systems.</p> </div> </td> </tr> </table> </div> </div> <div class="sect2"> <h3 id="at.spacecmd.api"><a class="anchor" href="#at.spacecmd.api"></a><a class="link" href="#at.spacecmd.api">api</a></h3> <div class="paragraph"> <p>The following API command and its options are available for calling the XML-RPC API directly. Calling the API directly allows you to use the latest features in SUSE Manager from the command-line using spacecmd as a wrapper for stand-alone commands or used from within scripts.</p> </div> <div class="admonitionblock note"> <table> <tr> <td class="icon"> <i class="fa icon-note" title="Note"></i> </td> <td class="content"> <div class="title">Use the api Command for Access to Latest Features</div> <div class="paragraph"> <p>spacecmd is the traditional tool for spacewalk. It functions out of the box with SUSE Manager but you should know that latest features (for example, Salt) are often excluded from traditional spacecmd command-line tool. To gain access to the latest feature additions call <code class="command">api api.getApiCallList</code> from within spacecmd to list all currently available API commands formatted in json. You can then call these commands directly.</p> </div> </td> </tr> </table> </div> <div class="dlist"> <dl> <dt class="hdlist1">api</dt> <dd> <p>Call XML-RPC API with arguments directly.</p> <div class="listingblock"> <div class="content"> <pre>usage: api [options] API_STRING

options: -A, --args Arguments for the API other than session id in comma separated strings or JSON expression -F, --format Output format -o, --output Output file

examples: api api.getApiCallList api --args "sysgroup_A" systemgroup.listSystems api -A "rhel-i386-server-5,2011-04-01,2011-05-01" -F "%(name)s" \ channel.software.listAllPackages</pre> </div> </div> </dd> </dl> </div> </div> <div class="sect2"> <h3 id="at.spacecmd.clear"><a class="anchor" href="#at.spacecmd.clear"></a><a class="link" href="#at.spacecmd.clear">clear</a></h3> <div class="paragraph"> <p>Clears the terminal screen</p> </div> </div> <div class="sect2"> <h3 id="at.spacecmd.clearcaches"><a class="anchor" href="#at.spacecmd.clearcaches"></a><a class="link" href="#at.spacecmd.clearcaches">clear_caches</a></h3> <div class="paragraph"> <p>Clear the internal caches kept for systems and packages</p> </div> <div class="listingblock"> <div class="content"> <pre>usage: clear_caches</pre> </div> </div> </div> <div class="sect2"> <h3 id="at.spacecmd.configchannel"><a class="anchor" href="#at.spacecmd.configchannel"></a><a class="link" href="#at.spacecmd.configchannel">configchannel_</a></h3> <div class="paragraph"> <p>The following spacecmd commands are available for use with configuration channels.</p> </div> <div class="dlist"> <dl> <dt class="hdlist1">configchannel_addfile</dt> <dd> <p>Creates a configuration file.</p> <div class="listingblock"> <div class="content"> <pre>usage: configchannel_addfile [CHANNEL] [options]

options: -c CHANNEL -p PATH -r REVISION -o OWNER [default: root] -g GROUP [default: root] -m MODE [defualt: 0644] -x SELINUX_CONTEXT -d path is a directory -s path is a symlink -b path is a binary (or other file which needs base64 encoding) -t SYMLINK_TARGET -f local path to file contents

  Note re binary/base64: Some text files, notably those containing trailing
  newlines, those containing ASCII escape characters (or other charaters not
  allowed in XML) need to be sent as binary (-b).  Some effort is made to auto-
  detect files which require this, but you may need to explicitly specify.</pre>
</div>
</div>
</dd>
<dt class="hdlist1">configchannel_backup</dt>
<dd>
<p>Backup a configuration channel.</p>
<div class="listingblock">
<div class="content">
<pre>usage: configchannel_backup CHANNEL [OUTDIR]

OUTDIR defaults to $HOME/spacecmd-backup/configchannel/YYYY-MM-DD/CHANNEL</pre> </div> </div> </dd> <dt class="hdlist1">configchannel_clone</dt> <dd> <p>Clone configuration channel(s).</p> <div class="listingblock"> <div class="content"> <pre>usage examples: configchannel_clone foo_label -c bar_label configchannel_clone foo_label1 foo_label2 -c prefix configchannel_clone foo_label -x "s/foo/bar" configchannel_clone foo_label1 foo_label2 -x "s/foo/bar"

options: -c CLONE_LABEL : name/label of the resulting cc (note does not update description, see -x option), treated as a prefix if multiple keys are passed -x "s/foo/bar" : Optional regex replacement, replaces foo with bar in the clone name, label and description Note : If no -c or -x option is specified, interactive is assumed</pre> </div> </div> </dd> <dt class="hdlist1">configchannel_create</dt> <dd> <p>Create a configuration channel.</p> <div class="listingblock"> <div class="content"> <pre>usage: configchannel_create [options]

options: -n NAME -l LABEL -d DESCRIPTION</pre> </div> </div> </dd> <dt class="hdlist1">configchannel_delete</dt> <dd> <p>Delete a configuration channel.</p> <div class="listingblock"> <div class="content"> <pre>usage: configchannel_delete CHANNEL …​</pre> </div> </div> </dd> <dt class="hdlist1">configchannel_details</dt> <dd> <p>Show the details of a configuration channel.</p> <div class="listingblock"> <div class="content"> <pre>usage: configchannel_details CHANNEL …​</pre> </div> </div> </dd> <dt class="hdlist1">configchannel_diff</dt> <dd> <p>Find differences between configuration channels.</p> <div class="listingblock"> <div class="content"> <pre>usage: configchannel_diff SOURCE_CHANNEL TARGET_CHANNEL</pre> </div> </div> </dd> <dt class="hdlist1">configchannel_export</dt> <dd> <p>Export configuration channel(s) to a json formatted file.</p> <div class="listingblock"> <div class="content"> <pre>usage: configchannel_export <CHANNEL>…​ [options] options: -f outfile.json : specify an output filename, defaults to <CHANNEL>.json if exporting a single channel, ccs.json for multiple channels, or cc_all.json if no CHANNEL specified e.g (export ALL)

Note : CHANNEL list is optional, default is to export ALL</pre> </div> </div> </dd> <dt class="hdlist1">configchannel_filedetails</dt> <dd> <p>Show the details of a file in a configuration Deltas: Dates can be expressed as delta values. For example, '2h' would mean 2 hours in the future. You can also use negative values to express times in the past (e.g., -7d would be one week ago).

Units: s -> seconds m -> minutes h -> hours d -> days</pre> </div> </div> </dd> <dt class="hdlist1">schedule_listarchived</dt> <dd> <p>List archived actions.</p> <div class="listingblock"> <div class="content"> <pre>usage: schedule_listarchived [BEGINDATE] [ENDDATE]

options: -u USERNAME -f FIRST_NAME -l LAST_NAME -e EMAIL -p PASSWORD --pam enable PAM authentication</pre> </div> </div> </dd> <dt class="hdlist1">user_delete</dt> <dd> <p>Delete an user.</p> <div class="listingblock"> <div class="content"> <pre>usage: user_delete NAME</pre> </div> </div> </dd> <dt class="hdlist1">user_details</dt> <dd> <p>Show the details of an user.</p> <div class="listingblock"> <div class="content"> <pre>usage: user_details USER …​</pre> </div> </div> </dd> <dt class="hdlist1">user_disable</dt> <dd> <p>Disable an user account.</p> <div class="listingblock"> <div class="content"> <pre>usage: user_disable NAME</pre> </div> </div> </dd> <dt class="hdlist1">user_enable</dt> <dd> <p>Enable an user account.</p> <div class="listingblock"> <div class="content"> <pre>usage: user_enable NAME</pre> </div> </div> </dd> <dt class="hdlist1">user_list</dt> <dd> <p>List all users.</p> <div class="listingblock"> <div class="content"> <pre>usage: user_list</pre> </div> </div> </dd> <dt class="hdlist1">user_listavailableroles</dt> <dd> <p>List all available roles for users.</p> <div class="listingblock"> <div class="content"> <pre>usage: user_listavailableroles</pre> </div> </div> </dd> <dt class="hdlist1">user_removedefaultgroup</dt> <dd> <p>Remove a default group from an user account.</p> <div class="listingblock"> <div class="content"> <pre>usage: user_removedefaultgroup USER <GROUP …​></pre> </div> </div> </dd> <dt class="hdlist1">user_removegroup</dt> <dd> <p>Remove a group to an user account.</p> <div class="listingblock"> <div class="content"> <pre>usage: user_removegroup USER <GROUP …​></pre> </div> </div> </dd> <dt class="hdlist1">user_removerole</dt> <dd> <p>Remove a role from an user account.</p> <div class="listingblock"> <div class="content"> <pre>usage: user_removerole USER ROLE</pre> </div> </div> </dd> <dt class="hdlist1">user_setemail</dt> <dd> <p>Set an user accounts email field.</p> <div class="listingblock"> <div class="content"> <pre>usage: user_setemail USER EMAIL</pre> </div> </div> </dd> <dt class="hdlist1">user_setfirstname</dt> <dd> <p>Set an user accounts first name field.</p> <div class="listingblock"> <div class="content"> <pre>usage: user_setfirstname USER FIRST_NAME</pre> </div> </div> </dd> <dt class="hdlist1">user_setlastname</dt> <dd> <p>Set an user accounts last name field.</p> <div class="listingblock"> <div class="content"> <pre>usage: user_setlastname USER LAST_NAME</pre> </div> </div> </dd> <dt class="hdlist1">user_setpassword</dt> <dd> <p>Set an user accounts name prefix field.</p> <div class="listingblock"> <div class="content"> <pre>usage: user_setpassword USER PASSWORD</pre> </div> </div> </dd> <dt class="hdlist1">user_setprefix</dt> <dd> <p>Set an user accounts name prefix field.</p> <div class="listingblock"> <div class="content"> <pre>usage: user_setprefix USER PREFIX</pre> </div> </div> </dd> </dl> </div> </div> <div class="sect2"> <h3 id="at.spacecmd.whoami"><a class="anchor" href="#at.spacecmd.whoami"></a><a class="link" href="#at.spacecmd.whoami">whoami</a></h3> <div class="paragraph"> <p>The following command is available for returning the currently logged spacecmd username.</p> </div> <div class="dlist"> <dl> <dt class="hdlist1">whoami</dt> <dd> <p>Print the currently logged spacecmd user.</p> <div class="listingblock"> <div class="content"> <pre>spacecmd {SSM:0}> whoami admin</pre> </div> </div> </dd> </dl> </div> </div> <div class="sect2"> <h3 id="at.spacecmd.whoamitalkingto"><a class="anchor" href="#at.spacecmd.whoamitalkingto"></a><a class="link" href="#at.spacecmd.whoamitalkingto">whoamitalkingto</a></h3> <div class="paragraph"> <p>The following spacecmd function is available for returning the server hostname.</p> </div> <div class="dlist"> <dl> <dt class="hdlist1">whoamitalkingto</dt> <dd> <p>Return the server hostname that spacecmd is connected with.</p> <div class="listingblock"> <div class="content"> <pre>spacecmd {SSM:0}> whoamitalkingto MGR_SERVER_HOSTNAME</pre> </div> </div> </dd> </dl> </div> </div> <div class="sect2"> <h3 id="at.spacecmd.misc.help.topics"><a class="anchor" href="#at.spacecmd.misc.help.topics"></a><a class="link" href="#at.spacecmd.misc.help.topics">Miscellaneous Help Topics</a></h3> <div class="paragraph"> <p>The following help topics are printed with all functions requiring the relevant information.</p> </div> <div class="dlist"> <dl> <dt class="hdlist1">time</dt> <dd> <p>Dates can be any of the following:</p> <div class="listingblock"> <div class="content"> <pre>Explicit Dates: Dates can be expressed as explicit date strings in the YYYYMMDD[HHMM] format. The year, month and day are required, while the hours and minutes are not; the hours and minutes will default to 0000 if no values are provided.

Deltas: Dates can be expressed as delta values. For example, '2h' would mean 2 hours in the future. You can also use negative values to express times in the past (e.g., -7d would be one week ago).

Units: s -> seconds m -> minutes h -> hours d -> days</pre> </div> </div> </dd> <dt class="hdlist1">systems</dt> <dd> <p><SYSTEMS> can be any of the following:</p> <div class="listingblock"> <div class="content"> <pre>name ssm (see 'help ssm') search:QUERY (see 'help system_search') group:GROUP channel:CHANNEL</pre> </div> </div> </dd> <dt class="hdlist1">ssm</dt> <dd> <p>The System Set Manager (SSM) is a group of systems that you</p> <div class="paragraph"> <p>can perform tasks on as a group.</p> </div> <div class="listingblock"> <div class="content"> <pre>Adding Systems: > ssm_add group:rhel5-x86_64 > ssm_add channel:rhel-x86_64-server-5 > ssm_add search:device:vmware > ssm_add host.example.com

Intersections: > ssm_add group:rhel5-x86_64 > ssm_intersect group:web-servers

Using the SSM: > system_installpackage ssm zsh > system_runscript ssm</pre> </div> </div> </dd> </dl> </div> </div> </div> </div>

<div class="sect1"> <h2 id="advanced.topics.app.ports.server"><a class="anchor" href="#advanced.topics.app.ports.server"></a><a class="link" href="#advanced.topics.app.ports.server">Uyuni Server</a></h2> <div class="sectionbody"> <div class="paragraph"> <p>Some ports are only relevant if you actually run the related service on the Uyuni server.</p> </div> <div class="dlist"> <div class="title">Ports to Open on UyuniServer</div> <dl> <dt class="hdlist1">67</dt> <dd> <p>Inbound / TCP/UDP / DHCP</p> <div class="paragraph"> <p>Required when Uyuni is configured as a DHCP server for systems requesting IP addresses.</p> </div> </dd> <dt class="hdlist1">69</dt> <dd> <p>Inbound / TCP/UDP / TFTP</p> <div class="paragraph"> <p>Used when Uyuni is configured as a PXE server and allows installation and re-installation of PXE-boot enabled systems.</p> </div> </dd> <dt class="hdlist1">80</dt> <dd> <p>Inbound / TCP / HTTP</p> <div class="paragraph"> <p>Client and proxy server requests travel via HTTP or HTTPS.</p> </div> </dd> <dt class="hdlist1">80</dt> <dd> <p>Outbound / TCP / HTTP</p> <div class="paragraph"> <p>Used to contact SUSE Customer Center/{ncc}.</p> </div> </dd> <dt class="hdlist1">443</dt> <dd> <p>Inbound / TCP / HTTPS</p> <div class="paragraph"> <p>All WebUI, client, and proxy server requests travel via HTTP or HTTPS.</p> </div> </dd> <dt class="hdlist1">443</dt> <dd> <p>Outbound / TCP / HTTPS</p> <div class="paragraph"> <p>Uyuni uses this port to reach SUSE Customer Center (unless running in a disconnected mode with RMT or SMT{mdash}as described in <a href="#disconnect-setup">[disconnect-setup]</a>).</p> </div> </dd> <dt class="hdlist1">5222</dt> <dd> <p>Inbound / TCP / osad</p> <div class="paragraph"> <p>When you wish to push actions to clients this port is required by the <code class="systemitem">osad</code> daemon running on your client systems.</p> </div> </dd> <dt class="hdlist1">5269</dt> <dd> <p>Inbound/Outbound / TCP / jabberd</p> <div class="paragraph"> <p>Needed if you push actions to or via a Uyuni Proxy.</p> </div> </dd> <dt class="hdlist1">4505</dt> <dd> <p>Inbound / TCP / salt</p> <div class="paragraph"> <p>Required by the Salt-master to accept communication requests via TCP from minions. The connection is initiated by the minion and remains open to allow the master to send commands. This port uses a publish/subscribe topology; the minion subscribes to notifications from the master.</p> </div> </dd> <dt class="hdlist1">4506</dt> <dd> <p>Inbound / TCP / salt</p> <div class="paragraph"> <p>Required by the Salt-master to accept communication requests via TCP from minions. The connection is initiated by the minion and is open only when needed. Usually, minions will open this port when they have to report results to the master, such as when a command received on port 4505 has finished. This port uses a request/response topology; the minion sends requests to the master.</p> </div> </dd> <dt class="hdlist1">25151</dt> <dd> <p>TCP</p> <div class="paragraph"> <p>For cobbler.</p> </div> </dd> </dl> </div> <div class="dlist"> <div class="title">Internally Used Ports on Uyuni Server</div> <dl> <dt class="hdlist1">2828</dt> <dd> <p>Internal /</p> <div class="paragraph"> <p>Satellite-search API, used by the RHN application in Tomcat and Taskomatic.</p> </div> </dd> <dt class="hdlist1">2829</dt> <dd> <p>Internal /</p> <div class="paragraph"> <p>Taskomatic API, used by the RHN application in Tomcat.</p> </div> </dd> <dt class="hdlist1">6868</dt> <dd> <p>Internal</p> <div class="paragraph"> <p>Auditlog-keeper to database.</p> </div> </dd> <dt class="hdlist1">6888</dt> <dd> <p>Internal</p> <div class="paragraph"> <p>Auditlog-keeper API, used by the RHN application in Tomcat.</p> </div> </dd> <dt class="hdlist1">8005</dt> <dd> <p>Internal</p> <div class="paragraph"> <p>Tomcat shutdown port.</p> </div> </dd> <dt class="hdlist1">8009</dt> <dd> <p>Internal</p> <div class="paragraph"> <p>Tomcat to Apache HTTPD (AJP).</p> </div> </dd> <dt class="hdlist1">8080</dt> <dd> <p>Internal</p> <div class="paragraph"> <p>Tomcat to Apache HTTPD (HTTP).</p> </div> </dd> <dt class="hdlist1">9080</dt> <dd> <p>Internal</p> <div class="paragraph"> <p>Salt-API, used by the RHN application in Tomcat and Taskomatic.</p> </div> </dd> <dt class="hdlist1">32000</dt> <dd> <p>Internal / TCP</p> <div class="paragraph"> <p>Port for a TCP connection to the Java Virtual Machine (JVM) that runs Taskomatic and the search (satellite-search).</p> </div> </dd> </dl> </div> <div class="admonitionblock note"> <table> <tr> <td class="icon"> <i class="fa icon-note" title="Note"></i> </td> <td class="content"> <div class="title">Ephemeral Ports</div> <div class="paragraph"> <p>Anything from port 32768 on (more exactly, what you can see with <code class="command">cat /proc/sys/net/ipv4/ip_local_port_range</code>) is an ephemeral port, typically used as the receiving end of a TCP connection. So if process A opens a TCP connection to process B (for example, port 22), then A chooses an arbitrary source TCP port to match with destination port 22.</p> </div> </td> </tr> </table> </div> <div class="paragraph"> <p>This image is a graphical representation of the ports used in Uyuni:</p> </div> <div class="imageblock"> <div class="content"> <img src="_images/ports_diagram.png" alt="ports diagram"> </div> </div> <div class="paragraph"> <p>Port 80 (http) is not used to serve the WebUI, and is closed in most installations. Port 80 is used temporarily for some bootstrap repositories and automated installations.</p> </div> </div> </div> <div class="sect1"> <h2 id="advanced.topics.app.ports.proxy"><a class="anchor" href="#advanced.topics.app.ports.proxy"></a><a class="link" href="#advanced.topics.app.ports.proxy">Uyuni Proxy Server</a></h2> <div class="sectionbody"> <div class="dlist"> <div class="title">Ports to Open on UyuniProxy Server</div> <dl> <dt class="hdlist1">22</dt> <dd> <p>Inbound /</p> <div class="paragraph"> <p>Required when using ssh-push or ssh-push-tunnel contact methods. Check-in on clients connected to a Uyuni Proxy will be initiated on the Uyuni Server and “hop through” through to clients.</p> </div> </dd> <dt class="hdlist1">80</dt> <dd> <p>Outbound /</p> <div class="paragraph"> <p>Used to reach Uyuni.</p> </div> </dd> <dt class="hdlist1">5222</dt> <dd> <p>Inbound / TCP</p> <div class="paragraph"> <p>For push actions and connections issued by <code class="systemitem">osad</code> running on the client systems.</p> </div> </dd> <dt class="hdlist1">5269</dt> <dd> <p>Inbound/Outbound / TCP</p> <div class="paragraph"> <p>For push actions with the server.</p> </div> </dd> </dl> </div> </div> </div> <div class="sect1"> <h2 id="advanced.topics.app.ports.client"><a class="anchor" href="#advanced.topics.app.ports.client"></a><a class="link" href="#advanced.topics.app.ports.client">Uyuni Client</a></h2> <div class="sectionbody"> <div class="dlist"> <div class="title">Ports to Open on Uyuni Client</div> <dl> <dt class="hdlist1">22</dt> <dd> <p>Inbound / SSH</p> <div class="paragraph"> <p>Required when using ssh-push or ssh-push-tunnel contact methods.</p> </div> </dd> <dt class="hdlist1">80</dt> <dd> <p>Outbound</p> <div class="paragraph"> <p>To reach the Uyuni server or Uyuni Proxy server.</p> </div> </dd> <dt class="hdlist1">5222</dt> <dd> <p>Outbound / TCP</p> <div class="paragraph"> <p>For push actions with the server or proxy server.</p> </div> </dd> </dl> </div> </div> </div>

<div id="preamble"> <div class="sectionbody"> <div class="paragraph"> <p>The AutoYaST profile in this section installs a SUSE Linux Enterprise Server system with all default installation options including a default network configuration using DHCP. After the installation is finished, a bootstrap script located on the Uyuni Uyuni server is executed in order to register the freshly installed system with Uyuni Uyuni. You need to adjust the IP address of the Uyuni Uyuni server, the name of the bootstrap script, and the root password according to your environment:</p> </div> <div class="listingblock"> <div class="content"> <pre><user> …​ <username>root</username> <user_password>`linux`</user_password> </user>

<location>http://192.168.1.1/pub/bootstrap/my_bootstrap.sh</location></pre> </div> </div> <div class="paragraph"> <p>The complete AutoYaST file:</p> </div> <div class="listingblock"> <div class="content"> <pre><?xml version="1.0"?> <!DOCTYPE profile> <profile xmlns="http://www.suse.com/1.0/yast2ns" xmlns:config="http://www.suse.com/1.0/configns"> <general> <mode> <confirm config:type="boolean">false</confirm> </mode> </general> <networking> <keep_install_network config:type="boolean">true</keep_install_network> </networking> <software> <install_recommended config:type="boolean">true</install_recommended> <patterns config:type="list"> <pattern>base</pattern> </patterns> </software> <users config:type="list"> <user> <encrypted config:type="boolean">false</encrypted> <fullname>root</fullname> <gid>0</gid> <home>/root</home> <password_settings> <expire></expire> <flag></flag> <inact></inact> <max></max> <min></min> <warn></warn> </password_settings> <shell>/bin/bash</shell> <uid>0</uid> <username>root</username> <user_password>linux</user_password> </user> </users> <scripts> <init-scripts config:type="list"> <script> <interpreter>shell</interpreter> <location>http://192.168.1.1/pub/bootstrap/my_bootstrap.sh</location>; </script> </init-scripts> </scripts> </profile></pre> </div> </div> <div class="paragraph"> <p>Use this enhancement fragment to add child channels:</p> </div> <div class="listingblock"> <div class="content"> <pre><add-on> <add_on_products config:type="list"> <listentry> <ask_on_error config:type="boolean">true</ask_on_error> <media_url>http://$c_server/ks/dist/child/channel-label/distribution-label</media_url> <name>$c_name</name> <product>$c_product</product> <product_dir>/</product_dir> </listentry> …​ </add_on_products> </add-on></pre> </div> </div> <div class="paragraph"> <p>Replace <code class="replaceable">channel-label</code> and <code class="replaceable">distribution-label</code> with the correct labels (such as <code>sles11-sp1-updates-x86_64</code> and <code>sles11-sp2-x86_64</code>). Ensure that the distribution label corresponds to the Autoinstallable Distribution. Set the variables (such as <code>$c_server</code>) according to your environment. For information about variables, see <a href="#">reference-webui-systems-autoinstallation.adoc#s4-sm-system-kick-dist-variables</a>.</p> </div> <div class="admonitionblock important"> <table> <tr> <td class="icon"> <i class="fa icon-important" title="Important"></i> </td> <td class="content"> <div class="title">Add the Updates Channel</div> <div class="paragraph"> <p>It is required that you add the updates tools channel to the <add-on> AutoYaST snippet section. This ensures your systems are provided with an up-to-date version of the <code>libzypp</code> package. If you do not include the updates tools channel, you will encounter <code>400</code> errors. In this example, the (DISTRIBUTION_NAME) is replaced with the name of the autoinstallation distribution, as created previously, from <span class="menuseq"><b class="menu">Systems</b> <i class="fa fa-angle-right caret"></i> <b class="submenu">Autoinstallation</b> <i class="fa fa-angle-right caret"></i> <b class="menuitem">Distributions</b></span></p> </div> <div class="listingblock"> <div class="content"> <pre><listentry> <ask_on_error config:type="boolean">true</ask_on_error> <media_url>http://$redhat_management_server/ks/dist/child/sles12-sp2-updates-x86_64/(DISTRIBUTION_NAME)</media_url>; <name>sles12 sp2 updates</name> <product>SLES12</product> <product_dir>/</product_dir> </listentry></pre> </div> </div> </td> </tr> </table> </div> </div> </div>
